### [134] [PerProb: Indirectly Evaluating Memorization in Large Language Models](https://arxiv.org/abs/2512.14600)
*Yihan Liao,Jacky Keung,Xiaoxue Ma,Jingyu Zhang,Yicheng Sun*

Main category: cs.CR

TL;DR: PerProb是一个统一的、无标签框架，用于间接评估大型语言模型的记忆漏洞，通过比较受害模型和攻击模型生成数据的困惑度和平均对数概率变化来间接估计训练引起的记忆，适用于黑盒和白盒设置。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 大型语言模型的快速发展依赖于包含敏感信息的大规模数据集，引发了严重的隐私担忧。成员推理攻击（MIA）是主要威胁之一，但现有研究存在不一致的发现和缺乏标准化评估方法的问题，且许多LLM训练集未公开，难以直接评估MIA影响。

Method: 提出PerProb框架，通过比较受害模型和攻击模型生成数据的困惑度和平均对数概率变化来间接评估模型记忆。该方法不依赖成员/非成员标签或内部访问，独立于模型和任务，适用于黑盒和白盒设置。系统地将MIA分为四种攻击模式进行评估。

Result: 在五个数据集上评估PerProb的有效性，揭示了不同LLM之间不同的记忆行为和隐私风险。评估了知识蒸馏、早停和差分隐私等缓解策略，证明这些方法能有效减少数据泄漏。

Conclusion: PerProb提供了一个实用且可推广的框架，用于评估和改进LLM的隐私保护。研究结果为理解LLM记忆行为和开发隐私保护技术提供了重要见解。

Abstract: The rapid advancement of Large Language Models (LLMs) has been driven by extensive datasets that may contain sensitive information, raising serious privacy concerns. One notable threat is the Membership Inference Attack (MIA), where adversaries infer whether a specific sample was used in model training. However, the true impact of MIA on LLMs remains unclear due to inconsistent findings and the lack of standardized evaluation methods, further complicated by the undisclosed nature of many LLM training sets. To address these limitations, we propose PerProb, a unified, label-free framework for indirectly assessing LLM memorization vulnerabilities. PerProb evaluates changes in perplexity and average log probability between data generated by victim and adversary models, enabling an indirect estimation of training-induced memory. Compared with prior MIA methods that rely on member/non-member labels or internal access, PerProb is independent of model and task, and applicable in both black-box and white-box settings. Through a systematic classification of MIA into four attack patterns, we evaluate PerProb's effectiveness across five datasets, revealing varying memory behaviors and privacy risks among LLMs. Additionally, we assess mitigation strategies, including knowledge distillation, early stopping, and differential privacy, demonstrating their effectiveness in reducing data leakage. Our findings offer a practical and generalizable framework for evaluating and improving LLM privacy.

</details>


<div id='cs.MA'></div>

# cs.MA [[Back]](#toc)

### [135] [Multi-Agent Collaborative Framework for Intelligent IT Operations: An AOI System with Context-Aware Compression and Dynamic Task Scheduling](https://arxiv.org/abs/2512.13956)
*Zishan Bai,Enze Ge,Junfeng Hao*

Main category: cs.MA

TL;DR: AOI是一个面向AI运维的多智能体协作框架，通过LLM上下文压缩器和三层内存架构解决云原生架构中的运维数据过载问题，显著提升运维效率和故障修复速度。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 云原生架构（微服务和动态编排）导致现代IT基础设施极其复杂和易变，产生海量运维数据，造成传统系统的关键瓶颈：信息处理效率低下、任务协调差、故障诊断和修复过程中上下文连续性丢失。

Method: 提出AOI（AI-Oriented Operations）多智能体协作框架，集成三个专门智能体与基于LLM的上下文压缩器。核心创新包括：(1) 基于实时系统状态自适应优先级的动态任务调度策略；(2) 三层内存架构（工作记忆、情景记忆、语义记忆）优化上下文保留和检索。

Result: 在合成和真实基准测试中，AOI有效缓解信息过载，实现72.4%的上下文压缩率，同时保留92.8%的关键信息；显著提升运维效率，达到94.2%的任务成功率，相比最佳基线将平均修复时间（MTTR）减少34.4%。

Conclusion: 这项工作提出了向可扩展、自适应和上下文感知的自主运维的范式转变，能够以最少的人工干预稳健管理下一代IT基础设施。

Abstract: The proliferation of cloud-native architectures, characterized by microservices and dynamic orchestration, has rendered modern IT infrastructures exceedingly complex and volatile. This complexity generates overwhelming volumes of operational data, leading to critical bottlenecks in conventional systems: inefficient information processing, poor task coordination, and loss of contextual continuity during fault diagnosis and remediation. To address these challenges, we propose AOI (AI-Oriented Operations), a novel multi-agent collaborative framework that integrates three specialized agents with an LLM-based Context Compressor. Its core innovations include: (1) a dynamic task scheduling strategy that adaptively prioritizes operations based on real-time system states, and (2) a three-layer memory architecture comprising Working, Episodic, and Semantic layers that optimizes context retention and retrieval. Extensive experiments on both synthetic and real-world benchmarks demonstrate that AOI effectively mitigates information overload, achieving a 72.4% context compression ratio while preserving 92.8% of critical information and significantly enhances operational efficiency, attaining a 94.2% task success rate and reducing the Mean Time to Repair (MTTR) by 34.4% compared to the best baseline. This work presents a paradigm shift towards scalable, adaptive, and context-aware autonomous operations, enabling robust management of next-generation IT infrastructures with minimal human intervention.

</details>


### [136] [Multi-Agent Medical Decision Consensus Matrix System: An Intelligent Collaborative Framework for Oncology MDT Consultations](https://arxiv.org/abs/2512.14321)
*Xudong Han,Xianglun Gao,Xiaoyi Qu,Zhenyu Yu*

Main category: cs.MA

TL;DR: 提出了一个基于多智能体大语言模型的医疗决策共识矩阵系统，通过7个专业角色模拟多学科团队会诊，使用Kendall一致性系数量化共识，结合强化学习优化决策质量，在多个医学基准测试中表现优异。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 当前多学科团队会诊缺乏结构化机制来量化共识和确保决策可追溯性，需要一种能够客观评估医疗决策共识并提供证据追溯的系统。

Method: 部署7个专业大语言模型智能体（肿瘤科医生、放射科医生、护士、心理学家、患者倡导者、营养师、康复治疗师）模拟真实MDT工作流程，采用基于Kendall一致性系数的共识矩阵量化共识，集成Q-Learning、PPO和DQN等强化学习方法优化决策质量和共识效率。

Result: 在5个医学基准测试（MedQA、PubMedQA、DDXPlus、MedBullets、SymCat）中平均准确率达到87.5%（基准为83.8%），共识达成率89.3%，平均Kendall's W系数0.823，专家评审临床适宜性评分8.9/10。

Conclusion: 该系统通过结构化共识测量、角色专业化多智能体协作和基于证据的可解释性，提高了临床决策的质量和效率，推动了医疗AI的发展。

Abstract: Multidisciplinary team (MDT) consultations are the gold standard for cancer care decision-making, yet current practice lacks structured mechanisms for quantifying consensus and ensuring decision traceability. We introduce a Multi-Agent Medical Decision Consensus Matrix System that deploys seven specialized large language model agents, including an oncologist, a radiologist, a nurse, a psychologist, a patient advocate, a nutritionist and a rehabilitation therapist, to simulate realistic MDT workflows. The framework incorporates a mathematically grounded consensus matrix that uses Kendall's coefficient of concordance to objectively assess agreement. To further enhance treatment recommendation quality and consensus efficiency, the system integrates reinforcement learning methods, including Q-Learning, PPO and DQN. Evaluation across five medical benchmarks (MedQA, PubMedQA, DDXPlus, MedBullets and SymCat) shows substantial gains over existing approaches, achieving an average accuracy of 87.5% compared with 83.8% for the strongest baseline, a consensus achievement rate of 89.3% and a mean Kendall's W of 0.823. Expert reviewers rated the clinical appropriateness of system outputs at 8.9/10. The system guarantees full evidence traceability through mandatory citations of clinical guidelines and peer-reviewed literature, following GRADE principles. This work advances medical AI by providing structured consensus measurement, role-specialized multi-agent collaboration and evidence-based explainability to improve the quality and efficiency of clinical decision-making.

</details>
